---
title: "k3b - major trouble burning anything"
date: 2009-05-11
forum: Multimedia Software
---

### Post by berilac on 2009-05-11
This has been an ongoing problem.

Originally once I setup k3b to work with mp3's, everything was fine.
Then it became temperamental. Sometimes it would burn, sometimes, not.
Then it would create coasters more often than not (after "successfully" completing the burn).

Since then, I have installed and removed and installed again, various codecs to do with audio and video (for various programs).

Now, k3b won't even begin the burn process...To illustrate my meaning as best as I can, you can see an error log below (from a cancelled process, as it just hangs at the point where it starts to actually burn to disc).

### Post by HappyFeet on 2009-05-11
When uninstalling and reinstalling, you must do the following, or it does no good.

Completely remove k3b in synaptic. Then do:
```
sudo apt-get clean && sudo apt-get autoremove
```
Then reinstall.

Also, does this happen with other burning apps, or just k3b?

---

### Post by NewDisciple on 2009-05-12
**Check in your package manager to see if wodim is installed.  This has happened to me in the past when wodim was somehow not installed.**

### Post by ashmew2 on 2009-05-13
On my jaunty , i checked the version of cdrecord , and it is an alpha (2.01.01a03)

The latest stable release was [B][COLOR=#006000]2.00.3 ..So i'd suggest downgrading cdrecord to that version ?

[COLOR=Black]Completely remove [/COLOR][/COLOR][/B][COLOR=#006000][COLOR=Black]Brasero/k3b/cdrecord/wodim , and then download the older version tarball from here :[/COLOR][/COLOR]
[ftp://ftp.berlios.de/pub/cdrecord/cdrtools-2.00.3.tar.gz](ftp://ftp.berlios.de/pub/cdrecord/cdrtools-2.00.3.tar.gz)

Its a complete suite with cdrecord and others..

Its worth a try , but you may break your dependencies...

And i think you shouldnt worry about the ubuntu-desktop package , but then again you could have broken dependencies..

---

### Post by berilac on 2009-05-13

should i still give the cdrecord downgrade a go, or consign myself over (well my dad, it's his computer) to purchasing a new writer?

---

### Post by ashmew2 on 2009-05-13
Edit : Aahhhhhh....I just read on your profile Display Pic that you are using Hardy Heron..and NOT Jaunty , so your cdrecord version must be the stable one then and not the alpha one!

So its an hardware issue after all then (i mean there's a chance now)..We've been bashing cdrecord and K3b for no reasons then hehe...Well i think its not worth the downgrade because sometimes those darn broken dependencies wont fix whatever you do...It's better that you get a new Rom , but before you go and buy one , I'd suggest borrowing one from a friend or something...So you can be sure that its your cd drive thats been defaulting all along ;)

### Post by NewDisciple on 2009-05-13

### Post by NewDisciple on 2009-05-13
[B]This is not the answer to your problem, but rather, what I have discovered in researching RLIMIT MEMLOCK.  The links I'm providing should give you enough information to redirect your questions in a different manner to someone who is more capable than I.
This is an old discussion regarding user groups: [http://linux.derkeiler.com/Mailing-Lists/Fedora/2007-06/msg02031.html]("http://linux.derkeiler.com/Mailing-Lists/Fedora/2007-06/msg02031.html")
Here is my usr/bin/group:
> usr/bin/groups
#!/bin/sh
# groups -- print the groups a user is in
# Copyright (C) 1991, 1997, 2000, 2002, 2004-2007 Free Software Foundation, Inc.

# This program is free software: you can redistribute it and/or modify
# it under the terms of the GNU General Public License as published by
# the Free Software Foundation, either version 3 of the License, or
# (at your option) any later version.

# This program is distributed in the hope that it will be useful,
# but WITHOUT ANY WARRANTY; without even the implied warranty of
# MERCHANTABILITY or FITNESS FOR A PARTICULAR PURPOSE.  See the
# GNU General Public License for more details.

# You should have received a copy of the GNU General Public License
# along with this program.  If not, see <http://www.gnu.org/licenses/>.

# Written by David MacKenzie <djm@gnu.ai.mit.edu>.

# Make sure we get GNU id, if possible; also allow
# it to be somewhere else in PATH if not installed yet.
PATH=/usr/bin:$PATH

usage="Usage: $0 [OPTION]... [USERNAME]...

  --help      display this help and exit
  --version   output version information and exit

Same as id -Gn.  If no USERNAME, use current process.

Report bugs to <bug-coreutils@gnu.org>."

version='groups (GNU coreutils) 6.10
Copyright (C) 2008 Free Software Foundation, Inc.
License GPLv3+: GNU GPL version 3 or later <http://gnu.org/licenses/gpl.html>
This is free software: you are free to change and redistribute it.
There is NO WARRANTY, to the extent permitted by law.

Written by David MacKenzie.'


for arg
do
  case $arg in
    --help | --hel | --he | --h)
      exec echo "$usage" ;;
    --version | --versio | --versi | --vers | --ver | --ve | --v)
      exec echo "$version" ;;
    --)
      shift
      break ;;
    -*)
      echo "$0: invalid option: $arg" >&2
      exit 1 ;;
    *)
      break ;;
  esac
done

# With fewer than two arguments, simply exec "id".
case $# in
  0|1) exec id -Gn -- "$@" ;;
esac

# With more, we need a loop, and be sure to exit nonzero upon failure.
status=0
write_error=0

for name
do
  if groups=`id -Gn -- "$name"`; then
    echo "$name : $groups" || {
      status=$?
      if test $write_error = 0; then
	echo "$0: write error" >&2
	write_error=1
      fi
    }
  else
    status=$?
  fi
done

exit $status

This is just to know info.

Now to the meat of the issue: RLIMIT MEMLOCK
[]("http://lkml.indiana.edu/hypermail/linux/kernel/0601.3/0414.html")

Definition: EUID: Expands to the effective user ID of the current user or process, initialized at shell startup. 

EUID rules: [http://www.linuxforums.org/forum/linux-security/41746-privilege-fsuid-s-privilege-decides-rwx-files-not-euids-decision.html](http://www.linuxforums.org/forum/linux-security/41746-privilege-fsuid-s-privilege-decides-rwx-files-not-euids-decision.html)

Here is where I left off in my research: []("http://www.google.com/linux?hl=en&q=euid&btnG=Search")

There is a ton of info at the last link I gave.  Anything further is beyond my experience or knowledge.  But as stated previously it should get you going in the right direction for better help than I can provide.
Good Luck![/B]
